MICROPILE INSTALLATION AND TESTING REPORT
MICROPILE FOUNDATIONS
EWA MALL EXPANSION
ALA MOANA CENTER
Dear Mr Haske
As requested Geolabs Inc provided geotechnical engineering observation and
consultation services during the micropile foundation installation for the above project
The following letter report summarizes our geotechnical engineering observations
during installation of the micropile foundations for the Ewa Mall Expansion project in
Honolulu on the Island of Oahu Hawaii The project location and general vicinity are
shown on the Project Location Map Plate 1
Geolabs provided geotechnical engineering consultation for the design of the
micropile foundation and our recommendations are presented in the report entitled
Geotechnical Engineering Exploration Ewa Mall Expansion Ala Moana Center
Honolulu Oahu Hawaii dated and subsequent modifications
during the project construction The purpose of our geotechnical engineering
observation during construction was to provide engineering consultation during the
construction of the micropile foundation and to provide Special Inspection services by
observing the micropile foundation installation and testing at the project for general
conformance with the project plans specifications and our recommendations
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS
In general the Ewa Mall Expansion project involves expansion of the western
Ewa end of the Ala Moana Center in Honolulu on the Island of Oahu Hawaii The project
area was formerly occupied by Sears department store and mall parking and will be
converted to four levels of retail development
General Growth Properties Inc
Page 2
W O Installation and Testing Report
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
Based on the anticipated subsurface conditions and structural loads a deep
foundation system consisting of augered cast in place ACIP piles was recommended to
reduce the potential for appreciable total and differential settlements from the structural
loads Due to accessibility and clearance considerations some of the renovation work
required the use of micropiles instead of ACIP piles
The scope of our work discussed in this letter report includes observation of the
micropile foundation construction for the Ewa Mall Expansion project only Hawaiian
Dredging Construction Company Inc HDCC is the general contractor for the project
and the micropile subcontractor is Kelikai Inc
SUBSURFACE CONDITIONS
The subsurface conditions at the project site consist of surface fill materials
overlying soft and or loose lagoonal deposits extending to depths of about 20 to 37 feet
below the existing pavement surface Below the highly compressible lagoonal deposits
coral ledges of variable thickness and hardness were generally encountered across the
project site The lagoonal deposits and or coral ledges were underlain by medium dense
coralline detritus materials with localized loose and dense zones extending to maximum
micropile installation depth of about 58 feet below the existing ground surface
We encountered groundwater at an elevation of about 0 feet Mean Sea Level
MSL at the time of the micropile installation Due to the proximity of the project site to the
Pacific Ocean water levels are expected to vary with tidal fluctuations It should be noted
that water levels also may vary with seasonal precipitation storm surge conditions
groundwater withdrawal and other factors
MICROPILE INSTALLATION
Geotechnical recommendations for the micropile foundations were presented in
Section Foundations of our geotechnical engineering report dated
The purpose of our geotechnical engineering observation and
consultation services was to observe the micropile foundation installation and testing for
general conformance with our recommendations
Based on the anticipated subsurface conditions at the site the micropiles were
specified to extend through the loose lagoonal deposits and derive load bearing support
from the coralline materials encountered at greater depths To achieve the allowable
compressive load capacity with a factor of safety of 2 the micropiles were specified to
extend a minimum of about 10 or 20 feet into the hard coral ledge and or dense
coralline materials in order to develop an allowable compressive load capacity of 40 or
80 kips respectively To reduce risk of micropile necking within the loose soft lagoonal
material permanent steel casing was specified to be left in place at the top of each
micropile
General Growth Properties Inc
Page 3
W O Installation and Testing Report
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
Static Load Test
As part of the construction requirements one static load test was conducted on a
sacrificial micropile to verify the design perimeters and evaluate the adequacy of the
foundation support system The results of the static load test are presented in our letter
report entitled Micropile Load Test Report Ewa Mall Expansion Ala Moana Center
Honolulu Oahu Hawaii dated
Production Micropiles
Kelikai Inc installed a total of 129 production micropiles from
through at the approximate locations shown on Plates 2 through 4
Details of the micropile installation are presented in the Micropile Installation Records in
Appendix A and summarized on Plates 5 1 through 5 3
In general the micropiles were installed using a TEI 75 or Beretta T59 rig
equipped with a bull rock under reamer advancing a 5 5 inch OD Outside Diameter
steel casing to the specified depth of the micropile to effectively create a drilled hole of
at least 5 5 inches Advancing steel casing to the bottom of the specified depth was
required in order to facilitate the micropile drilling and ensure the quality of the grouting
Air pressure up to 100 pounds per square inch psi was utilized during the drilling
operation to create a bulb around the drilling bit 4 inch diameter for advancing
temporary steel casing 5 5 inch O D
After the drilled holes were extended to the specified depth and cleaned out a
reinforcing bar Grade 150 all threaded 11 rebar or Grade 75 all threaded 10
depending on design load capacity was placed in the cased hole with centralizers
Grout was batched on site utilizing a colloidal high shear and high speed
mixer equipped with a grout pump The grout mix consisted of
one sack of 94 pound Portland Cement Type I and or pounds of masonry sand
and 5 gallons of water with a design 28 day compressive strength of 4 000 psi
The grout was placed in the cased hole through a 1 inch diameter PVC tremie
pipe starting from the bottom of the cased hole After sound grout appeared at the top of
the cased hole the temporary steel casing was removed one section 4 or 5 feet long
at a time until the bottom of the steel casing approached the tip of the permanent casing
elevation or the specified top of the grout bulb zone Positive grout in take was
maintained during the grouting operation No significant micropile necking was
indicated based on review of the micropile grouting records
General Growth Properties Inc
Page 4
W O Installation and Testing Report
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
Micropile Testing
In order to evaluate the load carrying capacities of the installed micropiles pullout
tests proof tests were conducted on a total of 10 production BM 73
DM 59 DM MP 14 and MP 26 In general the
micropiles were loaded to a maximum test load of 60 or 120 kips 150 percent of the
design load in increments equivalent to approximately 25 of the design load The
micropiles were held at each load increment for 5 minutes and held at the maximum test
load for 10 minutes to evaluate creep effects At the maximum test load the creep
movement during the holding period between 1 and 10 minutes was less than 0 04 inches
typically allowed for the ground anchor system for the tested micropiles Details of the
proof tests are presented in Appendix B and summarized in the table below

Based on our field observations and the proof tests conducted it is our
professional opinion that the specified micropiles for the project have been installed to
the required diameter and sufficient depths to achieve the design load capacity of 40 or
80 kips with a factor of safety of 2 0

LIMITATIONS
The results submitted herein are based in part upon our field observations and the
micropile proof tests performed during the micropile foundation installation work It should
be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities occurring
simultaneously on a construction site even when our representatives are on the project
site on a full time basis Our observation and consultation services were performed in
accordance with generally accepted standards of geotechnical engineering practice no
warranty is expressed or implied Provision of construction monitoring by an engineer is
not insurance nor does it guarantee construction of any type The contractor shall retain
primary responsibility for the quality of the work for adhering to plans and specifications
and for repairing defects regardless of when they are found
CLOSURE
We appreciate the opportunity to be of service to you on this project If you have
questions or need additional information please contact our office
Respectfully submitted
